  18. \\"Who would have thought a stretch mark cream would turn out to be the anti-wrinkle breakthrough of the decade!\\" <br /> <br />In a remarkable turn of events, arguably one of the strangest in the history of cosmetics, women across the country are putting a stretch-mark cream called Rejuvinol AM/PM on their face to diminish the appearance of fine lines, wrinkles and crows' feet. And, if consumer sales are any indication of a product's effectiveness, Rejuvinol AM/PM is nothing short of a miracle. Women, as well as a growing number of \\"Boomer\\" men, are buying so much Rejuvinol AM/PM that finding a tube at your local cosmetic counter has become just about impossible. Has everyone gone mad? Well...not really. <br /> <br />Scientific Breakthrough or Dumb Luck? <br />Although Rejuvinol AM/PM functional components were already backed by clinical trials documenting their ability to visibly reduce the appearance of existing stretch marks (prominent because of their depth, length, discoloration and texture)... the success of Rejuvinol AM/PM as an anti-wrinkle cream was \\"dumb luck,\\" says Rudy Gay, spokesperson for Dermalogics, Rejuvinol AM/PM manufacturer. <br /> <br />When we first handed out samples of the Rejuvinol AM/PM formula to employees and customers as part of our market research, the sample tubes were simply marked \\"topical cream\\" with the lot number underneath,\\" Mr. Gay explains. \\"As the samples were passed to friends and family, the message became a little muddled and some people used this \\"topical cream\\" as a facial moisturizer. As we began to receive feedback from users, like \\"I look 10 years younger\\" and \\"I can't even notice my crows' feet\\" we knew we had something more than America's most effective stretch-mark cream. The point was driven home as store owners began reporting that almost as many people were purchasing Rejuvinol as an anti-wrinkle cream as were buying it to reduce stretch marks.\\" <br /> <br />Dr. Steven Lebowitz, PhD, Dermalogic's Director ofScientific Affairs, says, \\"Clearly, people were seeing results, but we didn't have a scientific explanation as to why this wrinkle-reduction was occurring. However, based on the incredibly positive reports, I started using it myself applying Rejuvinol to my face after shaving.\\" Dr. Lebowitz adds, \\"On a personal note, my wife tells me I haven't looked this good in years.\\" <br /> <br />Dumb Luck Strikes Again! <br />Then, on Tuesday, July 2, 2003, at a meeting of the 20th World Congress of Dermatology in Paris, France, a series of studies detailing the superior wrinkle-reducing properties of a patented oligo-peptide \\"called Pal-KTTKS\\" versus retinol, vitamin C, and placebo, on \\"photo-aged skin\\" was presented.1,2 \\"As luck would have it,\\" Dr. Lebowitz states, \\"the anti-wrinkle oligo-peptide tested in the breakthrough clinical trials turned out to be a key ingredient in the Rejuvinol cream.\\" <br /> <br />In the trials, subjects applied the patented peptide solution to the crows' feet area on one side of the face, and a cream containing either retinol, vitamin C, or a placebo to the other side. <br /> <br />Subjects in the Pal-KTTKS/retinol study applied the cream once a day for 2 months and then twice a day for the next 2 months. Using special image analysis, the study's authors reported \\"significant improvement\\" in both the overall appearance of skin tone and wrinkles for those women using the peptide solution. <br /> <br />Better yet, at the 2-month halfway point, the peptide solution worked nearly 1.5 times faster than retinol \\"in measured parameters,\\" and without the inflammation retinol often causes in sensitive skin. As was expected, the results of the remaining studies confirmed that the Pal-KTTKS solution's effectiveness at reducing the appearance of fine lines and wrinkles far exceeded both vitamin C and placebo. <br /> <br />A smoother, younger complexion, with less irritation and faster results-all without expensive (and painful) peels, implants or injections. <br /> <br />Better than Retinol and Vitamin C, But Is Rejuvinol AM/PM Better than Botox? <br /> <br />Dr. Jennifer Cifelli, PhD, RD, Director of Women's Health at Minneapolis based Golden Sun Systems, exclusive distributor for Dermalogics, explains, \\"Leading dermatologists agree that Botox is the preferred treatment for moderate to severe frown lines between the brow. But ever since it was discovered that Rejuvinol could reduce the appearance of fine lines, wrinkles, and crows' feet... the kind of fine lines, wrinkles and crows feet that can add 10-15 years to your appearance and which costly medical treatments often leave behind... skin-care professionals have been recommending, and using, Rejuvinol.\\" <br /> <br />In fact, researchers believe non-invasive alternatives are better, because, Dr. Cifelli continues, \\"Topical creams and gels offer gradual, continual results, while the effects of injections, facial peels, and dermabrasions are rougher on the skin and wear off.\\" In other words, Rejuvinol AM/PM helps give you a youthful, healthy, glowing complexion faster than retinol, far superior to vitamin C, and without irritation, needles, or surgery. Even better, many dermatologists and plastic surgeons recommend Rejuvinol AM/PM in conjunction with cosmetic procedures, including Botox. <br /> <br />So, if you see someone applying an anti-stretch mark cream to their face, don't think they've gone off the deep end... they may be smarter than you think. <br />

  28. The quest for a Botox alternative is a popular pursuit among both skin care manufacturers and consumers. While Botox is highly effective in reducing motion wrinkles, it is expensive, requires physician-administered injections, and occasionally leads to side effects, such as droopy eyelids. Not surprisingly, products touted as Botox alternatives keep popping up. Acetyl hexapeptide-3 (trade name Argireline and main ingredient in REJUVINOL) is one of the seemingly promising new Botox alternatives. Argireline is manufactured by a Spanish company Lipotec and is a hexapeptide (a chain of 6 amino acids) attached to the acetic acid residue. It is believed to work by inhibiting the release of neurotransmitters. When applied to the skin, Argireline supposedly relaxes facial tension leading to the reduction in facial lines and wrinkles with regular use. This remotely resembles the effect of Botox, which reduces facial tension and movement by paralyzing facial muscles. Note that Argireline is unrelated in its physiologic effect and mechanism of action to other bioactive skin peptides, such as palmitoyl pentapeptide. So far, the evidence to support the benefits of Argireline is very promising. In a clinical study published in the International Journal of Cosmetic Science, acetyl hexapeptide-3 at a 10% concentration has been shown to reduce the depth of wrinkles up to 30% after 30 days of use and this is the amount used in the REJUVINOL formula. There are no other credible clinical studies to be found but many are being conducted. The benefits of long-term use, if any, are unknown but look good. Is it worth a try? The rationale behind REJUVINOL is plausible enough and eventually it may be validated by research as a safe and effective wrinkle fighter. However, at this point neither its effectiveness nor safety can be considered even tentatively proven. Besides, Argireline-based products are not particularly cheap, even compared to Botox. However, I am not sure if theirprices reflect a large novelty-hype premium or high costs of the concentrated (10% or more is required) active ingredient. If it's the former, the prices may eventually decline. There is one more concern worth mentioning. Botox injections target specific muscles, whereas Argireline (if it indeed works) is likely to relax most of your face. And while Argireline may reduce wrinkles, it may also, in theory, increase facial sag because the neurotransmitters whose release Argireline inhibits, help maintain facial firmness. Notably, a popular firming skin care ingredient DMAE firms by stimulating the release of neurotransmitters and increasing facial tension, i.e. by producing roughly the opposite effect to Argireline. Whether Argireline may indeed contribute to facial sag has not been studied. Until further research is done it is concluded that Rejuvinol is one of the top anti-wrinkle creams on the market and should be around for years to come!

Complications are rare but they do occur, ranging from scarring to fatalities. Plastic surgery may be particularly risky if you have certain health conditions (e.g. diabetes). <br /> <br />Everyone is different. Some people do much better than others, even when treated by the same plastic surgeon. <br /> <br />It may take several weeks or months before your face fully recovers from plastic surgery. <br /> <br />Plastic surgery might adversely affect the physiology of your skin and underlying tissues, speeding up the aging process. <br />If you decide to undergo plastic surgery, keep in mind the following. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />With plastic surgery, more is not necessarily better. For instance, too tight or too frequent facelifts may create a distorted, unnatural look. The result may be worse than having no plastic surgery at all. <br /> <br />Find a board certified surgeon with a vast experience in the plastic surgery. Search thoroughly, compare different plastic surgeons, talk to their former patients. <br /> <br />It is somewhat more risky to have plastic surgery in a surgeon's office than in a hospital. If you are having an in-office plastic surgery, make sure that the facility is accredited by AAAASF (The American Association for Accreditation of Ambulatory Surgery Facilities). <br /> <br />Plastic surgery does not slow down the aging of the skin but may actually accelerate it. Therefore, plastic surgery is not a substitute for skin rejuvenation measures discussed in various articles at Smart Skin Care Site.   42. <br /> <br />In a remarkable turn of events, arguably one of the strangest in the history of cosmetics, women across the country are putting a stretch-mark cream called Rejuvinol AM/PM on their face to diminish the appearance of fine lines, wrinkles and crows' feet. And, if consumer sales are any indication of a product's effectiveness, Rejuvinol AM/PM is nothing short of a miracle. Women, as well as a growing number of \\"Boomer\\" men, are buying so much Rejuvinol AM/PM that finding a tube at your local cosmetic counter has become just about impossible. Has everyone gone mad? Using special image analysis, the study's authors reported \\"significant improvement\\" in both the overall appearance of skin tone and wrinkles for those women using the peptide solution. <br /> <br />Better yet, at the 2-month halfway point, the peptide solution worked nearly 1.5 times faster than retinol \\"in measured parameters,\\" and without the inflammation retinol often causes in sensitive skin. Acetyl hexapeptide-3 (trade name Argireline and main ingredient in REJUVINOL) is one of the seemingly promising new Botox alternatives. <br /> <br />Argireline is manufactured by a Spanish company Lipotec and is a hexapeptide (a chain of 6 amino acids) attached to the acetic acid residue. It is believed to work by inhibiting the release of neurotransmitters. When applied to the skin, Argireline supposedly relaxes facial tension leading to the reduction in facial lines and wrinkles with regular use. This remotely resembles the effect of Botox, which reduces facial tension and movement by paralyzing facial muscles. Note that Argireline is unrelated in its physiologic effect and mechanism of action to other bioactive skin peptides, such as palmitoyl pentapeptide. <br /> <br />So far, the evidence to support the benefits of Argireline is very promising. In a clinical study published in the International Journal of Cosmetic Science, acetyl hexapeptide-3 at a 10% concentration has been shown to reduce the depth of wrinkles up to 30% after 30 days of use and this is the amount used in the REJUVINOL formula. There are no other credible clinical studies to be found but many are being conducted. The benefits of long-term use, if any, are unknown but look good. <br /> <br />Is it worth a try? The rationale behind REJUVINOL is plausible enough and eventually it may be validated by research as a safe and effective wrinkle fighter. However, at this point neither its effectiveness nor safety can be considered even tentatively proven. Besides, Argireline-based products are not particularly cheap, even compared to Botox. However, I am not sure if their prices reflect a large novelty-hype premium or high costs of the concentrated (10% or more is required) active ingredient. If it's the former, the prices may eventually decline. <br /> <br />There is one more concern worth mentioning. Botox injections target specific muscles, whereas Argireline (if it indeed works) is likely to relax most of your face. And while Argireline may reduce wrinkles, it may also, in theory, increase facial sag because the neurotransmitters whose release Argireline inhibits, help maintain facial firmness. Notably, a popular firming skin care ingredient DMAE firms by stimulating the release of neurotransmitters and increasing facial tension, i.e. by producing roughly the opposite effect to Argireline. Whether Argireline may indeed contribute to facial sag has not been studied. Until further research is done it is concluded that Rejuvinol is one of the top anti-wrinkle creams on the market and should be around for years to come! <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />

  66. The quest for a Botox alternative is a popular pursuit among both skin care manufacturers and consumers. While Botox is highly effective in reducing motion wrinkles, it is expensive, requires physician-administered injections, and occasionally leads to side effects, such as droopy eyelids. Not surprisingly, products touted as Botox alternatives keep popping up. Acetyl hexapeptide-3 (trade name Argireline and main ingredient in REJUVINOL) is one of the seemingly promising new Botox alternatives. <br /> <br />Argireline is manufactured by a Spanish company Lipotec and is a hexapeptide (a chain of 6 amino acids) attached to the acetic acid residue. It is believed to work by inhibiting the release of neurotransmitters. When applied to the skin, Argireline supposedly relaxes facial tension leading to the reduction in facial lines and wrinkles with regular use. This remotely resembles the effect of Botox, which reduces facial tension and movement by paralyzing facial muscles. Note that Argireline is unrelated in its physiologic effect and mechanism of action to other bioactive skin peptides, such as palmitoyl pentapeptide. <br /> <br />So far, the evidence to support the benefits of Argireline is very promising. In a clinical study published in the International Journal of Cosmetic Science, acetyl hexapeptide-3 at a 10% concentration has been shown to reduce the depth of wrinkles up to 30% after 30 days of use and this is the amount used in the REJUVINOL formula. There are no other credible clinical studies to be found but many are being conducted. The benefits of long-term use, if any, are unknown but look good. <br /> <br />Is it worth a try? The rationale behind REJUVINOL is plausible enough and eventually it may be validated by research as a safe and effective wrinkle fighter. However, at this point neither its effectiveness nor safety can be considered even tentatively proven. Besides, Argireline-based products are not particularly cheap, even compared to Botox. However, I am not sure if their prices reflect a large novelty-hype premium or high costs of the concentrated (10% or more is required) active ingredient. If it's the former, the prices may eventually decline. <br /> <br />There is one more concern worth mentioning. Botox injections target specific muscles, whereas Argireline (if it indeed works) is likely to relax most of your face. And while Argireline may reduce wrinkles, it may also, in theory, increase facial sag because the neurotransmitters whose release Argireline inhibits, help maintain facial firmness. Notably, a popular firming skin care ingredient DMAE firms by stimulating the release of neurotransmitters and increasing facial tension, i.e. by producing roughly the opposite effect to Argireline. Whether Argireline may indeed contribute to facial sag has not been studied.   70. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />The quest for a Botox alternative is a popular pursuit among both skin care manufacturers and consumers. While Botox is highly effective in reducing motion wrinkles, it is expensive, requires physician-administered injections, and occasionally leads to side effects, such as droopy eyelids. Not surprisingly, products touted as Botox alternatives keep popping up. Acetyl hexapeptide-3 (trade name Argireline and main ingredient in REJUVINOL) is one of the seemingly promising new Botox alternatives. <br /> <br />Argireline is manufactured by a Spanish company Lipotec and is a hexapeptide (a chain of 6 amino acids) attached to the acetic acid residue. It is believed to work by inhibiting the release of neurotransmitters. When applied to the skin, Argireline supposedly relaxes facial tension leading to the reduction in facial lines and wrinkles with regular use. This remotely resembles the effect of Botox, which reduces facial tension and movement by paralyzing facial muscles. Note that Argireline is unrelated in its physiologic effect and mechanism of action to other bioactive skin peptides, such as palmitoyl pentapeptide. <br /> <br />So far, the evidence to support the benefits of Argireline is very promising. In a clinical study published in the International Journal of Cosmetic Science, acetyl hexapeptide-3 at a 10% concentration has been shown to reduce the depth of wrinkles up to 30% after 30 days of use and this is the amount used in the REJUVINOL formula. There are no other credible clinical studies to be found but many are being conducted. The benefits of long-term use, if any, are unknown but look good. <br /> <br />Is it worth a try? The rationale behind REJUVINOL is plausible enough and eventually it may be validated by research as a safe and effective wrinkle fighter. However, at this point neither its effectiveness nor safety can be considered even tentatively proven. Besides, Argireline-based products arenot particularly cheap, even compared to Botox. However, I am not sure if their prices reflect a large novelty-hype premium or high costs of the concentrated (10% or more is required) active ingredient. If it's the former, the prices may eventually decline. <br /> <br />There is one more concern worth mentioning. Botox injections target specific muscles, whereas Argireline (if it indeed works) is likely to relax most of your face. And while Argireline may reduce wrinkles, it may also, in theory, increase facial sag because the neurotransmitters whose release Argireline inhibits, help maintain facial firmness. Notably, a popular firming skin care ingredient DMAE firms by stimulating the release of neurotransmitters and increasing facial tension, i.e. by producing roughly the opposite effect to Argireline. Whether Argireline may indeed contribute to facial sag has not been studied. Until further research is done it is concluded that Rejuvinol is one of the top anti-wrinkle creams on the market and should be around for years to come! <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />

Plastic Surgery Facts <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />What You Should Know about the Risks and Benefits of Plastic Surgery. <br /> <br />Topical treatments can help improve fine wrinkles and skin texture. However, rapid and dramatic improvements are more likely to be achieved with plastic surgery. But don't rush to schedule your plastic surgery just yet. First, here are some facts you should know. <br /> <br /> <br />Plastic surgery is expensive. In the US, a facelift costs from $6,000 to $12,000. <br /> <br />Any surgery is potentially dangerous, including plastic surgery. Complications are rare but they do occur, ranging from scarring to fatalities. Plastic surgery may be particularly risky if you have certain health conditions (e.g. diabetes). <br /> <br />Everyone is different. Some people do much better than others, even when treated by the same plastic surgeon. <br /> <br />It may take several weeks or months before your face fully recovers from plastic surgery. <br /> <br />Plastic surgery might adversely affect the physiology of your skin and underlying tissues, speeding up the aging process. <br />If you decide to undergo plastic surgery, keep in mind the following. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />With plastic surgery, more is not necessarily better. For instance, too tight or too frequent facelifts may create a distorted, unnatural look. The result may be worse than having no plastic surgery at all. <br /> <br />Find a board certified surgeon with a vast experience in the plastic surgery. Search thoroughly, compare different plastic surgeons, talk to their former patients. <br /> <br />It is somewhat more risky to have plastic surgery in a surgeon's office than in a hospital. If you are having an in-office plastic surgery, make sure that the facility is accredited by AAAASF (The American Association for Accreditation of Ambulatory Surgery Facilities). <br /> <br />Plastic surgery does not slow down the aging of the skin but may actually accelerateit. Therefore, plastic surgery is not a substitute for skin rejuvenation measures discussed in various articles at Smart Skin Care Site. Actually, after a plastic surgery you should be even more diligent in preserving your skin's youth. <br /> <br />Before going for plastic surgery, give a few month try to topical skin rejuvenation treatments (see Treatments section of this site). The results may be dramatic enough to change your mind. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />

The results may be dramatic enough to change your mind. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />
  96. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />I have found the Rejuvinol system to be excellent. I am experiencing great moisturiztion on the skin and an overall tighter and firmer complexion. I did research on the active ingredient argiriline and not surprisingly the medical information on it really good. It was quite surprising maybe you will find it helpful. <br /> <br />Argireline is the name of the molecule acetyl hexapeptide-3. When applied topically, Argireline seems to have an effect similar to that of BOTOX injections on the muscles of the face. Peptides are small fragments of proteins. Proteins are the main building blocks of nearly all living tissues. Argireline, acetyl hexapeptide-3, is a chain of six amino acids that are attached to the residue of acetic acid. Topical application of Argireline is the only method of delivery that as yet has been tested. <br />Argireline relaxes facial tension, leading to the relaxation of facial muscles that contribute to lines and wrinkles. Researchers think Argireline works by inhibiting the release of neurotransmitters released by the brain that tell these facial muscles to tense. The result is relaxed musculature and reduced wrinkles and lines. The Argireline's effects are very similar to those of BOTOX injections. But where the FDA only allows BOTOX serum to be injected in limited areas of the face, Argireline may be applied wherever lines and wrinkles appear. One published study showed a 30% reduction in wrinkle size after only 30 days of using Argireline or its generic equivalent, acetyl hexapeptide-3.Yes. Argireline is one of the most exciting ingredients to come along in recent years. Argireline works on mechanical lines and tension-related wrinkles and therefore makes an excellent combination with other, more traditional, anti wrinkle ingredients that work by resurfacing and moisturizing the skin.Argireline is a favorable and promising alternative to botox injections and one that is highly recommended when foundin anti aging skin care products that have additional effective ingredients. Look for Argireline or acetyl hexapeptide-3 in the ingredients before you buy. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />

  98. The quest for a Botox alternative is a popular pursuit among both skin care manufacturers and consumers. While Botox is highly effective in reducing motion wrinkles, it is expensive, requires physician-administered injections, and occasionally leads to side effects, such as droopy eyelids. Not surprisingly, products touted as Botox alternatives keep popping up. Acetyl hexapeptide-3 (trade name Argireline and main ingredient in REJUVINOL) is one of the seemingly promising new Botox alternatives. <br /> <br />Argireline is manufactured by a Spanish company Lipotec and is a hexapeptide (a chain of 6 amino acids) attached to the acetic acid residue. It is believed to work by inhibiting the release of neurotransmitters. When applied to the skin, Argireline supposedly relaxes facial tension leading to the reduction in facial lines and wrinkles with regular use. This remotely resembles the effect of Botox, which reduces facial tension and movement by paralyzing facial muscles. Note that Argireline is unrelated in its physiologic effect and mechanism of action to other bioactive skin peptides, such as palmitoyl pentapeptide. <br /> <br />So far, the evidence to support the benefits of Argireline is very promising. In a clinical study published in the International Journal of Cosmetic Science, acetyl hexapeptide-3 at a 10% concentration has been shown to reduce the depth of wrinkles up to 30% after 30 days of use and this is the amount used in the REJUVINOL formula. There are no other credible clinical studies to be found but many are being conducted. The benefits of long-term use, if any, are unknown but look good. <br /> <br />Is it worth a try? The rationale behind REJUVINOL is plausible enough and eventually it may be validated by research as a safe and effective wrinkle fighter. However, at this point neither its effectiveness nor safety can be considered even tentatively proven. Besides, Argireline-based products are not particularly cheap, even compared to Botox. However, I am not sure if their prices reflect a large novelty-hype premium or high costs of the concentrated (10% or more is required) active ingredient. If it's the former, the prices may eventually decline. <br /> <br />There is one more concern worth mentioning. Botox injections target specific muscles, whereas Argireline (if it indeed works) is likely to relax most of your face. And while Argireline may reduce wrinkles, it may also, in theory, increase facial sag because the neurotransmitters whose release Argireline inhibits, help maintain facial firmness. Notably, a popular firming skin care ingredient DMAE firms by stimulating the release of neurotransmitters and increasing facial tension, i.e. by producing roughly the opposite effect to Argireline. Whether Argireline may indeed contribute to facial sag has not been studied. Until further research is done it is concluded that Rejuvinol is one of the top anti-wrinkle creams on the market and should be around for years to come! <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />

Well...not really. <br /> <br />Scientific Breakthrough or Dumb Luck? <br />Although Rejuvinol AM/PM functional components were already backed by clinical trials documenting their ability to visibly reduce the appearance of existing stretch marks (prominent because of their depth, length, discoloration and texture)... the success of Rejuvinol AM/PM as an anti-wrinkle cream was \\"dumb luck,\\" says Rudy Gay, spokesperson for Dermalogics, Rejuvinol AM/PM? manufacturer. <br /> <br />When we first handed out samples of the Rejuvinol AM/PM formula to employees and customers as part of our market research, the sample tubes were simply marked \\"topical cream\\" with the lot number underneath,\\" Mr. Gay explains. \\"As the samples were passed to friends and family, the message became a little muddled and some people used this \\"topical cream\\" as a facial moisturizer. The point was driven home as store owners began reporting that almost as many people were purchasing Rejuvinol as an anti-wrinkle cream as were buying it to reduce stretch marks.\\" <br /> <br />Dr. Steven Lebowitz, PhD, Dermalogic's Director of Scientific Affairs, says, \\"Clearly, people were seeing results, but we didn't have a scientific explanation as to why this wrinkle-reduction was occurring. However, based on the incredibly positive reports, I started using it myself applying Rejuvinol to my face after shaving.\\" Dr. Lebowitz adds, \\"On a personal note, my wife tells me I haven't looked this good in years.\\" <br /> <br />Dumb Luck Strikes Again! <br />Then, on Tuesday, July 2, 2003, at a meeting of the 20th World Congress of Dermatology in Paris, France, a series of studies detailing the superior wrinkle-reducing properties of a patented oligo-peptide \\"called Pal-KTTKS\\" versus retinol, vitamin C, and placebo, on \\"photo-aged skin\\" was presented.1,2 \\"As luck would have it,\\" Dr. Lebowitz states, \\"the anti-wrinkle oligo-peptide tested in the breakthrough clinical trials turned out to be a key ingredient in the Rejuvinol cream.\\" <br /> <br />In the trials, subjects applied the patented peptide solution to the crows' feet area on one side of the face, and a cream containing either retinol, vitamin C, or a placebo to the other side. <br /> <br />Subjects in the Pal-KTTKS/retinol study applied the cream once a day for 2 months and then twice a day for the next 2 months. Using special image analysis, the study's authors reported \\"significant improvement\\" in both the overall appearance of skin tone and wrinkles for those women using the peptide solution. <br /> <br />Better yet, at the 2-month halfway point, the peptide solution worked nearly 1.5 times faster than retinol \\"in measured parameters,\\" and without the inflammation retinol often causes in sensitive skin. As was expected, the results of the remaining studies confirmed that the Pal-KTTKS solution's effectiveness at reducing the appearance of fine lines and wrinkles far exceeded both vitamin C and placebo. <br /> <br />A smoother, younger complexion, with less irritation and faster results-all without expensive (and painful) peels, implants or injections. <br /> <br />Better than Retinol and Vitamin C, But Is Rejuvinol AM/PM Better than Botox? <br /> <br />Dr. Jennifer Cifelli, PhD, RD, Director of Women's Health at Minneapolis based Golden Sun Systems, exclusive distributor for Dermalogics, explains, \\"Leading dermatologists agree that Botox is the preferred treatment for moderate to severe frown lines between the brow. But ever since it was discovered that Rejuvinol could reduce the appearance of fine lines, wrinkles, and crows' feet... the kind of fine lines, wrinkles and crows feet that can add 10-15 years to your appearance and which costly medical treatments often leave behind... skin-care professionals have been recommending, and using, Rejuvinol.\\" <br /> <br />In fact, researchers believe non-invasive alternatives are better, because, Dr. Cifelli continues, \\"Topical creams and gels offer gradual, continual results, while the effects of injections, facial peels, and dermabrasions are rougher on the skin and wear off.\\" In other words, Rejuvinol AM/PM helps give you a youthful, healthy, glowing complexion faster than retinol, far superior to vitamin C, and without irritation, needles, or surgery.   137. What You Should Know about the Risks and Benefits of Plastic Surgery. <br /> <br />Topical treatments can help improve fine wrinkles and skin texture. However, rapid and dramatic improvements are more likely to be achieved with plastic surgery. But don't rush to schedule your plastic surgery just yet. First, here are some facts you should know. <br /> <br /> <br />Plastic surgery is expensive. In the US, a facelift costs from $6,000 to $12,000. <br /> <br />Any surgery is potentially dangerous, including plastic surgery. Complications are rare but they do occur, ranging from scarring to fatalities. Plastic surgery may be particularly risky if you have certain health conditions (e.g. diabetes). <br /> <br />Everyone is different. Some people do much better than others, even when treated by the same plastic surgeon. <br /> <br />It may take several weeks or months before your face fully recovers from plastic surgery. <br /> <br />Plastic surgery might adversely affect the physiology of your skin and underlying tissues, speeding up the aging process. <br />If you decide to undergo plastic surgery, keep in mind the following. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />With plastic surgery, more is not necessarily better. For instance, too tight or too frequent facelifts may create a distorted, unnatural look. The result may be worse than having no plastic surgery at all. <br /> <br />Find a board certified surgeon with a vast experience in the plastic surgery. Search thoroughly, compare different plastic surgeons, talk to their former patients. <br /> <br />It is somewhat more risky to have plastic surgery in a surgeon's office than in a hospital. If you are having an in-office plastic surgery, make sure that the facility is accredited by AAAASF (The American Association for Accreditation of Ambulatory Surgery Facilities). <br /> <br />Plastic surgery does not slow down the aging of the skin but may actually accelerate it. Therefore, plastic surgery is not a substitute for skin rejuvenation measures discussed in various articles at Smart Skin Care Site. Actually, after a plastic surgery you should be even more diligent in preserving your skin's youth. <br /> <br />Before going for plastic surgery, give a few month try to topical skin rejuvenation treatments (see Treatments section of this site). The results may be dramatic enough to change your mind. <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br />

It was quite surprising maybe you will find it helpful. <br /> <br />Argireline is the name of the molecule acetyl hexapeptide-3. When applied topically, Argireline seems to have an effect similar to that of BOTOX injections on the muscles of the face. Peptides are small fragments of proteins. Proteins are the main building blocks of nearly all living tissues. Argireline, acetyl hexapeptide-3, is a chain of six amino acids that are attached to the residue of acetic acid. Topical application of Argireline is the only method of delivery that as yet has been tested. <br />Argireline relaxes facial tension, leading to the relaxation of facial muscles that contribute to lines and wrinkles. Researchers think Argireline works by inhibiting the release of neurotransmitters released by the brain that tell these facial muscles to tense. The result is relaxed musculature and reduced wrinkles and lines. The Argireline's effects are very similar to those of BOTOX injections. But where the FDA only allows BOTOX serum to be injected in limited areas of the face, Argireline may be applied wherever lines and wrinkles appear. One published study showed a 30% reduction in wrinkle size after only 30 days of using Argireline or its generic equivalent, acetyl hexapeptide-3.Yes. Argireline is one of the most exciting ingredients to come along in recent years. Argireline works on mechanical lines and tension-related wrinkles and therefore makes an excellent combination with other, more traditional, anti wrinkle ingredients that work by resurfacing and moisturizing the skin.Argireline is a favorable and promising alternative to botox injections and one that is highly recommended when found in anti aging skin care products that have additional effective ingredients. This causes many \\"Baby Boomers\\" to <br />exhibit an intense interest in procedures and techniques to help <br />them look as young and fit as they feel. <br /> <br />This is the point at which many Americans consider plastic <br />surgery. Signs of aging on the face are the most common <br />symptoms causing people to seek out plastic surgery. The four <br />most common facial complaints are: <br /> <br />Loose skin: The areas on the face where we see loose skin most <br />often are the jowls, the neck and the skin around the eyes. <br /> <br />Fine Lines: Tiny wrinkles on the face increase in number with <br />time and are more plentiful in lighter skinned people. The most <br />common sites are around the mouth and eyes but they can also <br />develop anywhere on the face. These lines are made worse by the <br />sun. <br /> <br />Bagginess around the eyes: Loose skin is only one of the causes <br />of bagginess around the eyes. Additionally, small fat pads <br />around the eyes can move from the top and sides of the eye <br />region and end up resting beneath the eyes. Shadows emphasize <br />the problem and if there is any inherited darkening of the skin <br />the problem becomes even more noticeable. <br /> <br />Exaggeration of Features: As we age, some of our features <br /> <br />continue to grow. Although the rate of growth is unperceivable <br />year toyear, eventually, over time we can see that there is an <br />actual lengthening of our earlobes and nose. Our brow may have <br />lowered and there is an increase of fat below the chin, and in <br />the fold between the nose and upper lip. <br /> <br />All of these complaints can be addressed through plastic <br />surgery. The success, risks and benefits differ depending on <br />the areas of the face and neck the surgery is to correct, as <br />well as other factors such as the age of the patient and the <br />severity of the problem. <br /> <br />What is a facelift? The facelift is the classical surgical <br />response to aging problems of the face and neck. In a facelift <br />the skin is separated from the underlying tissue and pulled <br />upwards and backwards. The excess skin is them removed <br />resulting in a lifting and tightening of the appearance of the <br />skin. <br /> <br />There are varying procedures that go deeper, some as far down <br />as the layer adjacent to the facial bones. Surgeons determine <br />how deep to go with the procedure based on the needs of the <br />patient, on a case by case basis. <br /> <br />What results can you expect from a facelift?: A facelift will <br />lift the areas of your face that are sagging, such as your <br />cheeks and jowls. It will also tighten the loose skin on your <br />neck as well as remove excess fat from under your chin and <br />alleviate that \\"turkey neck\\" look. <br /> <br />What about scarring? The scars from a facelift can be <br />extensive, although not easily detectable. Scars will more than <br />likely extend from above the ear, down the front of the ear, <br />around the ear lobe, up the back of the ear, and into the <br />hairline behind the ear. There can be another incision beneath <br />the chin. <br /> <br />Most scars from a facelift are hard to see once they heal. <br />Scars can be camouflaged with make-up within three weeks and <br />should fade beyond detection in one to three months. <br />What complications can occur? Some of the complications that <br />can result from a facelift are: Hematoma, Skin death; facial <br />weakness or paralysis; attached earlobe (pixie ear) and open ear <br />canal. <br /> <br />What about lines and wrinkles? Although the results of a <br />facelift and other facial plastic surgery can be dramatic the <br />signs of aging that a facelift will not alleviate are wrinkles <br />and fine lines on your face. Additional procedures such as Botox <br />Cosmetic(tm), laser resurfacing, chemical peels and dermabrasion of <br />the face are needed to address lines and wrinkle. <br /> <br />Is there a safer alternative to facelifts and other invasive <br />procedures? Amazing advances have been made recently in topical <br />preparations to combat the signs of aging. These topical <br />preparations are a safe alternatives to many of the invasive <br />procedures detailed above. They <br />report that the product diminish the appearance of forehead <br />creases, droopy brows, crow's feet, furrows, laugh lines, <br />feathered lips, and more. Additionally, it reduces the <br />appearance of acne scars, stretch marks, Rosacea, and enlarged <br />pores.
